Convexity is the single most important structural property in optimi…","domain":"foundations","level":"intermediate","type":"mixed","tags":["foundational","ml","optimization","theory","wiki-import","path-core-foundations","path-architectures"],"prerequisites":[],"related":["gradient-descent","lagrange-multipliers","stochastic-gradient-descent-sgd","ordinary-least-squares-ols-closed-form-solution"],"updatedAt":"2026-04-15","sourceDeck":"Machine Learning by Henrik Nordberg","papers":[{"citation":"Classical mathematics · Modern treatment: Boyd & Vandenberghe, Convex Optimization (2004)"}],"sections":[{"kind":"prose","body":"<p>A function whose epigraph (the region above its graph) is a convex set, equivalently one for which any chord between two points on the graph lies on or above the graph. Convexity is the single most important structural property in optimization: it guarantees that every local minimum is a global minimum and that gradient descent converges to it.</p><p><b>Definition.</b> A function \\( f : \\mathbb{R}^n \\to \\mathbb{R} \\) is convex if, for all \\( \\mathbf{x}, \\mathbf{y} \\) in its domain and all \\( t \\in [0, 1] \\):</p>\n\n  \\[ f\\bigl(t\\mathbf{x} + (1-t)\\mathbf{y}\\bigr) \\le t\\,f(\\mathbf{x}) + (1-t)\\,f(\\mathbf{y}) \\]\n\n  <p>If the inequality is strict for \\( \\mathbf{x} \\ne \\mathbf{y} \\) and \\( t \\in (0,1) \\), the function is <b>strictly convex</b>, which guarantees a unique global minimum.</p>"},{"kind":"prose","title":"Illustration","body":"$4"},{"kind":"prose","body":"<p><b>Second-order characterization.</b> If \\( f \\) is twice differentiable, it is convex if and only if its Hessian is positive semi-definite everywhere:</p>\n\n  \\[ \\nabla^2 f(\\mathbf{x}) \\succeq 0 \\quad \\forall\\, \\mathbf{x} \\]\n\n  <p>For strictly convex: \\( \\nabla^2 f(\\mathbf{x}) \\succ 0 \\) (positive definite).</p>"},{"kind":"prose","body":"<p><b>First-order characterization.</b> For differentiable \\( f \\), convexity is equivalent to the tangent line being a global underestimator:</p>\n\n  \\[ f(\\mathbf{y}) \\ge f(\\mathbf{x}) + \\nabla f(\\mathbf{x})^\\top (\\mathbf{y} - \\mathbf{x}) \\quad \\forall\\, \\mathbf{x}, \\mathbf{y} \\]\n\n  <p>This is why gradient descent works: the gradient always points toward lower function values, and there are no misleading local minima.</p>"},{"kind":"prose","title":"Examples in ML","body":"<ul>\n    <li><b>Convex losses:</b> Mean Squared Error, cross-entropy (w.r.t. linear model outputs), hinge loss, logistic loss</li>\n    <li><b>Convex regularizers:</b> L1 norm (convex, not strictly), L2 norm squared (strictly convex)</li>\n    <li><b>Non-convex:</b> deep neural network loss surfaces (composition with nonlinear activations destroys convexity)</li>\n  </ul>"},{"kind":"prose","body":"<p><b>Operations preserving convexity:</b> non-negative weighted sums, pointwise maximum, affine composition \\( f(Ax + b) \\). These rules let us verify convexity of composite objectives without computing Hessians.</p>"}],"cards":[{"noteId":"convex-function-q1","prompt":"Write the definition of convexity as a chord inequality, and state what strict convexity additionally guarantees.","answer":"\\( f(tx + (1-t)y) \\le t f(x) + (1-t) f(y) \\) for all \\( x, y \\) in the domain and \\( t \\in [0,1] \\). Strict convexity (strict inequality for \\( x \\neq y \\), \\( t \\in (0,1) \\)) additionally guarantees a unique global minimum. Without strictness, a convex function can have a flat minimum plateau (e.g., L1 norm).","tags":["foundational","ml","optimization","theory","wiki-import","path-core-foundations","path-architectures"]},{"noteId":"convex-function-q2","prompt":"State the second-order characterisation of convexity for a twice-differentiable function.","answer":"\\( f \\) is convex iff its Hessian \\( \\nabla^2 f(x) \\succeq 0 \\) (positive semi-definite) everywhere in the domain. Strictly convex: \\( \\nabla^2 f(x) \\succ 0 \\) (positive definite). For single variable: convex iff \\( f''(x) \\ge 0 \\) everywhere.","tags":["foundational","ml","optimization","theory","wiki-import","path-core-foundations","path-architectures"]},{"noteId":"convex-function-q3","prompt":"Why is the cross-entropy loss convex in a logistic regression's weights but not in a deep neural network's weights?","answer":"Logistic regression: logits are linear in \\( w \\) (\\( z = w^\\top x \\)), and cross-entropy composed with an affine function of weights remains convex. Deep neural network: the hidden activations nest nonlinearities (ReLU, sigmoid) inside the affine maps, so the composition is not affine in the weights. Composition of a convex function with a non-affine function is generally non-convex — deep loss surfaces have many local minima, saddle points.","tags":["foundational","ml","optimization","theory","wiki-import","path-core-foundations","path-architectures"]},{"noteId":"convex-function-q4","prompt":"Name four operations that preserve convexity, and use them to show \\( f(x) = \\|Ax - b\\|_2^2 + \\lambda \\|x\\|_1 \\) is convex.","answer":"Operations: (1) non-negative weighted sum, (2) pointwise max, (3) affine composition \\( f(Ax+b) \\), (4) composition with monotone convex outer function. For the example: \\( \\|x\\|_2^2 \\) is convex, so \\( \\|Ax - b\\|_2^2 \\) is convex by affine composition; \\( \\|x\\|_1 \\) is convex (sum of \\( |x_i| \\)); non-negative weighted sum of two convex
